## Introductory Section

The insurance sector in Saudi Arabia serves as a fundamental pillar to develop a resilient economy, given its pivotal role in preventing material losses and mitigating financial risks for businesses, individuals, alike.
With the establishment of Vision 2030, insurance has emerged as a key partner in the Quality of Life Program, improving service standards and introducing innovative insurance products. High legislative and regulatory standards in the country have enabled the sector to explore new horizons.Taking advantage of the vitality and constant evolution of this sector, MEDGULF provides customized services tailored to each client's needs. The company is committed to its mission and offers an array of innovative insurance solutions designed to meet the needs of various industries. These solutions include health and life insurance as well as general insurance, vehicles, and reinsurance, ensuring comprehensive coverage and compliance with client requirements.

Chairman's Message:

At this time last year, the company was at a historic inflection point where the board took actions to work on stabilizing and restoring the confidence in the company and its market position and what it is best at; managing the risk of its customers. At this specific point, we had a very stable company operationally where all claims were met as normal, making leads for new businesses and issuing new insurance policies. In fact, the brand and the position of the company were not in question, cementing the board views that the foundations of the company are strong and what was needed is the leadership that can make the transformation strategy work but with a strong focus and best allocation of resources. The board trusted that MEDGULF's CEO with his experience in the industry and MEDGULF, can make the turnaround a reality.

The new leadership took quick but thoughtful actions as follows:
1Making sure that the current clients are fully served with enough
and quality allocation of resources that can assure proactive
approaches.

2Rationalize and optimize the decision making with regards to the new business leads that reflect both the industry dynamics, our positioning and our capabilities.

3Working on a refreshed strategy that is inclusive of state of art strategy build up practices such as the involvement of across level management along with working inside out and the reverse strategy capitalizing on data and market experience feedback loop.

4Optimize the balance sheet that can support the daily business
but with strategic risk and solvency management.
With these initiatives and others, the company finished the year of
2023 with strong operational results. The solvency ratio increased
from just below 15% to more than 77%. The insurance revenue
increased by 26% to reach more than SAR 3.33 billion reflecting
the strength of the company's market position and the trust of our
clients and insured's members. Along with other healthy indicators,
the company recorded a historic net income of SAR 201.5 million
which is the highest for the company since 2012.

During the year, the company made significant progress in multiple business areas. For the digitization strategy, the company continues to add resources and technology across the value chain in Health, Motor and General insurance from the underwriting to the customer experience, feedback loop and reconciliations. The rationalized implementation strategy will capitalize on localization

of the technology with an open architecture that benefits from
strategic industry partnerships approach.

We have made as well strategic investments in the branding and marketing that will add value to the business and customer experience with the signing of the sponsorship agreement with Roshn Saudi League.

As a recognition of the company's positive progress, MEDGULF
won the Great Place to Work Certificate, the fastest insurance
company to getting the qualification of being shariah compliant
company and the best workplace in the Saudi insurance sector
from the International Finance Awards..

On the Human Resources side, the company attracted key executive profiles who are expected to deliver on the long-term objectives of the company. To build on the partnerships' signed the recent years, the company started 2024 with the start of the Youth Future program that is targeted to build the next generation of leadership in the company.

The Board of Directors and Management is optimistic now more
than ever about the company in specific and the insurance industry
in general driven by KSA vision 2030.

The industry environment is still very attractive in the long run and the commitment to build a competing and value-added player is still very strong. The last few years has been volatile and the risks associated with the dynamics in the market have been challenging. However, the company has been able to keep its market share with the current and the planned built up of capabilities are being utilized to exploit the market opportunities and hence, the value creation for our valued stakeholders.

Lastly, The Company, its Board of Directors and its Executive Management would like to express their deep appreciation and gratitude to the Custodian of the Two Holy Mosques and the Crown Prince for the great governmental support and help to improve the insurance sector in the Kingdom of Saudi Arabia. Great appreciation also is extended to the regulatory and supervisory institutions namely, the Saudi Central Bank, the Insurance Authority and the Council of Cooperative Health Insurance, who provide their guidance and support continuously.

Thanks are due as well to the Company's shareholders and our
valued clients for the continued trust in MEDGULF, and we look
forward to providing the best in the next financial year.

## Rakan Abdullah Abunayyan

Chairman of the Board

Terminology

- Annual Report: Adocument the company creates to provide essential information about its activities and financial performance during the previous year. It includes details about revenues, expenses, profits, losses, assets, liabilities, objectives, challenges, and opportunities.

-Statement of Income: A statement that shows the company's revenues and expenses over a period of time. It helps to determine the net profit (revenue) and net loss (expenses). The income statement is issued annually, quarterly, or monthly.

- **Statement of financial Posrition**: Astatement that indicates the company's assets, liabilities, and equity on a specific date. It helps to evaluate the company's financial capacity, flexibility, and stability. The balance sheet is issued annually, quarterly, or monthly.

- **Cash Flow Statement:** A statement that outlines the inflows and outflows of the company during a defined period to help analyze its ability to generate and manage cash. The cash flow statement is issued annually, quarterly, or monthly.

- CEO's Message: Astatement prepared by the company's executive management for shareholders, investors, and stakeholders interested in the annual report. It provides an overview of the company's performance, achievements, challenges, vision, and strategy. It conveys confidence, optimism, and stresses the company's commitment to values and social responsibility.

: figure]

[FIGURE: logo: MEDGULF
ميدغلف
Blue text with an abstract symbol resembling three arches within a square outline, all above a thin line]

- **Shareholders**: Individuals or entities that own a stake in the company's capital, receive profits, participate in significant decision-making, and receive dividends if applicable.

- **Operational Expenses**: Expenses arising from the company's daily activities, including salaries, rents, supplies, marketing, and others, affecting the company's net profit.

- **Profitability**: A measure of the company's ability to generate profits from revenues after deducting all expenses, reflecting the efficiency and success of the company. It is calculated using indicators such as profit margin, return on assets, and return on equity.

- Risks: These include factors or circumstances that jeopardize the company's ability to accomplish its objectives or sustainability, including financial, operational, legal, and strategic risks. They necessitate the development of strategies and policies to manage or mitigate them.

- **Social Responsibility**: It is the company's commitment to contribute to improving the environment, society, and the human resources working within it. The company undertakes initiatives and activities related to environmental conservation, equality, diversity, transparency, ethics, and values.

# Executive Summary

The Mediterranean Cooperative Insurance and Reinsurance Company (MEDGULF) is a listed joint-stock company providing a wide range of cooperative insurance and reinsurance services. The company provides services to over a million clients across the Kingdom and through a trained and qualified workforce operating with cutting-edge technologies.

Achievements:
This year, MedGulf achieved various milestones, and received numerous awards, including the Fastest
Growing Company in Shariah-Compliant Award and the Best Work Environment Award from the International
Finance Awards, along with the Best Workplace Environment Award.

The year also saw MEDGULF participating in several local and international forums. It also sponsored various events and initiatives, such as the 'Empowerment Forum' exhibition under the sponsorship of the Riyadh Chamber of Commerce, the Tuwaiq Employment Program, and the ROSHN Saudi Pro League as the Gold Sponsor.

The company continued to launch its educational and social programs, including the MEDGULF Nextgen program under the MEDGULF Academy to support new graduates. Additionally, it launched the HiPo program, the Graduate and Future Financial Leaders Development Program, as well as the LinkedIn Learning Initiative and analysis of training need and the digital library.

## Challenges:

The insurance market in Saudi Arabia is experiencing fierce competition and is undergoing regulatory, technological, and social changes. Like its counterparts, MEDGULF faces challenges in sustaining its growth and profitability under these circumstances.

To overcome these challenges, MEDGULF has adopted a strategy centered on three pillars in order to become the leading insurance company in the region:

*
Improving the efficiency and quality of operations, services, products, and human and financial resources.
*
Innovation and Digital Transformation: Utilizing modern technology and smart solutions to develop innovative, customized, and flexible insurance solutions that meet the needs and expectations of clients.
*
Expansion and Diversification: Increasing the company's market share, reaching new customer segments, and leveraging emerging opportunities in local and regional markets.

  3. &quot;Insurance revenues reached to SAR 3.33 billion during 2023, compared to SAR 2.64 billion 2022, with difference of an increase in revenue SAR 689 million and a growth rate of 26.07%.&quot;
  4. MEDGULF&#x27;s gross written premiums reached SAR 3.135 billion during 2023, compared to SAR 2.854 billion
  5. MEDGULF&#x27;s earnings per share amounted to SAR 1.92 in 2023, compared to SAR (3.78) in 2022
  6. MEDGULF&#x27;s financial solvency improved to 77%, an improvement of more than 64 percentage points compared to December 31, 2022
  7. MEDGULF achieved an increase in net investment income by SAR 89.7 million compared to the previous year
  8. The Insurance services result increased SAR 672.2 million in 2023, compared to 2022
  9. MEDGULF achieved strong performance in medical insurance, growing by 32.75%, along with increased insurance during 2023 compared to 2022

# MEDGULF in a Year

As of 2023, Medical Operations handled 2.4 million claims through automated processes, of which 990K were in Q4.

As of January 2024, the claims adjudication process is 99% automated for outpatient Nphies claims through a live API integration with an 'on premises' AI servers, along with automated price checking, benefits and limits allocation until claims settlement. This was all accomplished in collaboration with the IT application team and our partner TachyHealth.

Launch of the new Motor Claims Management System: Last year, MEDGULF successfully implemented a new Motor Claims Management System, which transformed how we handle claims processing and streamlined our operations. This system has enabled us to track and manage claims efficiently, improving response time and customer satisfaction.

Revamping and Deploying New Processes and Architectures: MEDGULF has embarked on an important initiative to revamp our processes and architectures. Through careful planning and implementation, we have successfully deployed new strategies and frameworks that improve workflow efficiency and resource utilization. This revamp has given us greater flexibility and adaptability in meeting evolving business requirements.

MEDGULF has introduced innovative surveying and investigation tools and devices, especially iPads, to enhance capabilities. These devices have enabled our specialists to conduct comprehensive and accurate on-site assessments, enabling faster decision-making and improving the overall claims management process.

CEO's Message:

I am pleased to express my sincere gratitude to all our
shareholders and employees whose dedication and hard
work have contributed to MEDGULF's remarkable success
in 2023.

With immense pride, I am pleased to announce that
MEDGULF Saudi Arabia Insurance Company has achieved
exceptional financial results that have exceeded our
expectations and targets.

At the year-end, our profits amounted to SAR 201.5
million, compared to losses of SAR 396.9 million incurred
during the same period in 2022. Insurance revenues also
increased during this year by SAR 689 million compared
to the previous year, with an increase rate of 26.07%. This
is primarily attributed to the growth in total insurance
premiums subscribed, amounting to SAR 280.9 million, -
GWP is SAR 3.135 billion. with a growth rate of 9.84%, driven
by the strong performance of medical insurance, which grew
by .75%, in addition to a significant portion from vehicle
insurance realized during 2023 from the 2022 activities.

The growth in insurance revenue led to positive results for
insurance services, reaching SAR 309.91 million compared
to losses of SAR 263.29 million in 2022, while net insurance
profits increased to SAR 87 million.

Solvency coverage ratios improved significantly to over
77%, an increase of more than 64 percentage points
compared to December 31, 2022. The company also saw
an increase in net investment income by SAR 89.7 million
compared to the previous year.

These outstanding results stem from the company's strategic
direction and the support provided by the Board of Directors.
Adherence to the International Financial Reporting Standard
in line with the standards adopted in Saudi Arabia

had an impact on presenting financial results and reassessing
similar periods of previous years.

A key contributor to our success was the significant improvement in our underwriting performance during 2023. This enabled us to offer our customers optimal insurance solutions, while exploiting current market opportunities.

Our financial performance was further strengthened by the diversification of our investment portfolio, which yielded higher returns through investments in low-risk, high-yield financial instruments. We also benefited from the overall improvement in financial markets.

In 2023, we actively engaged in social responsibility and initiatives, along with programs that benefit society. We prioritized the work environment given its crucial role in the company's success. This was reflected in our winning multiple awards this year in this regard, such as the Best Work Environment Award at the Finance Awards ceremony and the "Great Place to Work" Certificate award from Great Place To Work.

We celebrated National Day and Foundation Day with pride
and honor, as well as Social Responsibility Day and attended
a workshop hosted by the Ministry of Municipal and Rural
Affairs and Housing, aligned with the Kingdom's Vision

## There are numerous other initiatives are detailed in

this report as well.

Our achievements serve as a testament to our unwavering
dedication to excellence, quality, and innovation. However,
we remain driven to reach even greater heights. As we move
forward, with your continued support and the help of Allah,
we will be able to embark on new frontiers and achieve even
greater accomplishments.

Umar Al-Mahmoud

* Analyze business growth and status of current IT infrastructure and IT development plans to determine necessary requirements and provide recommendations for a scalable and maintainable IT infrastructure that enables it to achieve the required performance objectives in acost-effective and timely manner.

Strategic View:

MEDGULF has identified the following areas of focus as part of its strategic planning process:

- To position the company as a strong competitor in the insurance and underwriting market by implementing operational strategies and approaches that are designed to achieve profit margins that exceed industry benchmarks across various insurance lines.
- To distinguish the company through its unique business model, people model, and comprehensive suite of high-value services for customers, insured members, and stakeholders.
- To embrace innovation and align with market trends to develop a cutting-edge healthcare system.
- To establish a diversified marketing model with tailored offerings for each segment.
- Transitioning to a better model for human capital by separating systematic work and delivering professional services.

Company Overview:
About MEDGULF:
The Mediterranean and Gulf Cooperative Insurance and Reinsurance Company, MEDGULF, is a listed Saudi joint stock company registered in KSA under Commercial Registry No. 1010231925, providing insurance solutions for all products and businesses.

It is one of the largest and oldest insurance companies in the Kingdom, MEDGULF employs over 800 employees serving more than 1.5 million Saudi citizens and residents in the country.

[FIGURE: logo: MEDGULF
ميدغلف MEDGULF

* Pillars and Enablers:

- Partnership
This is MEDGULF's go-to-market strategy. It defines our customer base, product/service offerings & servicing tailored to each segment within the 3 major lines of business.
- Core
This is MEDGULF's backbone in terms of core systems. It takes an active role as a depository for MG's most valuable asset - its data.

- Operating Systems and Tools
These are the applications, systems, or methodologies that help operate effectively, maintain a competitive position, and improve performance.

- Interfaces
This defines how MEDGULF manages & governs its interfacing with internal & external products & services. These will serve as an intermediary for exchanging data (Enterprise Service Bus)

- Mindset
It defines MEDGULF's DNA - The MEDGULF Way. This defines the way "How" we do things at MEDGULF. Focus is on customers, break silos, improve collaboration and empower staff to make decisions and deliver faster.

- Discipline
This defines the set of rules & guidelines to support our effectiveness and improve quality of decision making on how we do business. It provides clarity on expected behaviors and supports accountability.

## Our Products:

MEDGULF offers a wide range of insurance products across its branches, providing extensive coverage for a variety of insurance products, including:

• Health Insurance:
MEDGULF is a leading provider of group health insurance in Saudi Arabia, with a team that is highly specialized
and extensively experienced in this field.

As part of their services, the company also offers a visa insurance policy for individuals, with benefits such as emergency medical coverage, travel delay coverage, baggage loss insurance and personal accident insurance.

The company also offers a variety of group insurance packages and categories tailored to meet the needs of institutions, ensuring the provision of appropriate services and healthcare for the insured and their families. These products address healthcare services according to the coverage system issued by the Council of Health Insurance.

In addition, MEDGULF provides extensive coverage for service providers throughout the Kingdom, with an insurance e-card for each member, electronic linkage for approvals, and value-added services to improve service accessibility. These services are available in the field around the clock.

## Motor Third Party Liability Insurance

It covers only third-party liability, protecting vehicles from legal liability resulting from accidents that cause bodily injury or damage to third-party property.

*
**Marine Insurance:**

This type of insurance provides comprehensive protection for cargo and ship hulls. It covers all kinds of damage or loss to cargo or ships.

It offers comprehensive coverage for external and internal property, and offers insurance solutions based on the following requirements:

**Goods Transportation Insurance (Single Shipment/Trip):**
The Land Transit Insurance (Single Shipment/Trip) covers the loss of goods during land transportation.
The policy covers the shipment of goods on a single trip between two points in order to protect against
maritime losses or navigational risks.

MEDGULF's insurance covers goods transported via ships, airplanes, vehicles, trucks, and railways.
There may be more than one type of transportation method required, especially if the transport is
international.

<!-- PAGE BREAK -->

[FIGURE: logo: MEDGULF

# MEDGULF

The logo features the company name in English and Arabic, with a stylized book icon on the left and a thin line underneath the text.]

Land Transit Insurance (Open Cover/Annual):

The Land Transit Insurance (Open Cover/Annual) covers losses or damage incurred by goods during transit. The insurance policy provides coverage for a period of one year or until the agreed date.

MEDGULF provides insurance coverage against risks associated with the transportation of goods via vehicles,
trucks, and railways.

Marine Cargo Insurance (Single Shipment/Trip):
The Marine Cargo Insurance (Single Shipment/trip) covers losses or damages occurring to goods during transportation from one place to another, with the insurance period limited to a single shipment/trip to protect against maritime losses or navigational risks. MEDGULF insures goods transported by ships, airplanes, vehicles, trucks, and railways. More than one type of transportation method may be required, especially international ones.

Marine Cargo Insurance (Open Cover/Annual):
Marine cargo insurance is coverage for losses or damages affecting goods during transport from one place to another, with the insurance period extending for one year or within the agreed-upon period to cover maritime losses or navigational risks. MEDGULF insures transported goods via ships, airplanes, vehicles, trucks, and railways. It may be necessary to use more than one type of transportation, especially when moving internationally.

## Marine Hull Insurance

The Marine Hull Insurance policy provides coverage and protection against the risks that may be encountered by the ship while on cruise between ports, while staying in ports during docking operations, or while in construction or building in a shipyard. The insurance covers all risks that the ship may encounter during a specified period of time (one year or during a certain voyage).

The marine hull insurance covers marine risk, which arise from navigation or is related to the sea. It also covers the dangers of the sea, such as ship sinking, stranding and maritime collisions caused by bad weather conditions such as fires, explosions, and piracy.

* Property Insurance:
The Property Insurance policy provides protection for owned or leased property and its contents against risks and damages caused by accidents, natural disasters, or thefts. You can rest assured that your business is covered in case of damage or loss caused by incidents that disrupt normal operations. Having adequate property insurance protects companies and ensures their success for the long term.

1Comprehensive Property Risk Insurance:
The Comprehensive Property Risk Insurance provides coverage against all types of risks to the property, including loss, destruction, damage, or any unforeseen events that may cause harm to the property.

This type of insurance can provide protection for your investments and is an indispensable insurance policy.

2Fire and Related Risks Insurance:
The Fire and Related Risks Insurance policy provides coverage against damage or loss caused by unforeseen events such as fires, lightning, earthquakes, floods, storms, or other disasters.

This insurance is designed to protect companies from financial losses resulting from property damage or loss due to these risks.

3Insurance against Terrorism and Sabotage Risks:
The Insurance Against Terrorism and Sabotage Risks policy covers against acts of sabotage and terrorism to protect the insured Against financial losses directly resulting from politically motivated acts of violence, acts of terrorism, and acts of sabotage.

4Political Violence Insurance:
The Political Violence Insurance policy covers against unrecoverable revenue or costs incurred due to unforeseen disruptions caused by political violence.

• Liability and General Accident Insurance:
The Liability and General Accident Insurance policy provides compensation against any unforeseen expenses, legal fees, and damages that may arise from accidents and other incidents. It covers a wide range of accidents, including slips and falls, property damage, product liability, among others. MEDGULF offers a range of products in this area, including:

1Employee Fraud Coverage Insurance:
The Bank Insurance policy is specifically designed to cover losses resulting from fraudulent activities by employees. It offers a wide range of coverage options to protect against various damages.

2Jewelry Insurance:
The Jewelry Insurance policy provides comprehensive coverage for gold and jewelry traders against a range of risks and protects their inventory of gold, jewelry, precious stones, and other valuables against theft, manipulation, and fraud.

3Fidelity Insurance:
The Fidelity Inusrance policy protects against financial losses resulting from theft or misuse of funds. It covers financial and material losses resulting from theft, embezzlement, forgery, or money fraud.

4Civil Liability Insurance:
The Civil Liability Insurance policy compensates for the value of legal liability that the insured must pay to a third party due to claims against accidental death or bodily injury, as well as any loss or damage to others' property in the course of the professional activities of the insured.

5Employers Liability Insurance:
The Employers Liability Insurance policy protects directors and executives against potential claims arising from their decisions and actions made within their daily duties, ensuring seamless operation for the business.

6Workers' Compensation Insurance:
The Workers' Compensation Insurance policy provides coverage for work-related accidents and illnesses, including death, permanent or temporary disability. It can be obtained independently or added to a compensation plan in accordance with labor and employment regulations, and MEDGULF covers all related costs.

Aviation Insurance:
The Aviation Insurance policy is designed to meet the unique needs of MEDGULF clients by providing multiple specialized coverage options for component manufacturers and airport operators, with insurance solutions that include:

1Aircraft Hull and Liability Insurance:

The Aircraft Hull and Liability Insurance policy covers losses or damage to the aircraft body or its parts, and liability for damages to others' property or injury to others. It also covers passenger injury or loss of life, damage or loss of personal belongings, baggage, or cargo, in addition to risks arising during flight or on the ground, as well as personal accidents occurring to the crew or passengers and war risks.

2Airport Contractors' Liability Insurance:
The Airport Contractors' Liability Insurance policy coverage is designed to protect against the loss or damage of aircraft or third-party property and/or occurrence of death or bodily injury to a third party, also to address the operations executed by the insured at the airport, making sure the airport is protected from any unexpected accidents that may occur.

3Unmanned Aerial Vehicle (Drone) Insurance:
The Unmanned Aerial Vehicle (Drone) Insurance policy provides coverage against any damages or losses arising from the use of drones and other unmanned aerial vehicles. There are three sections to this type of coverage:
- Material damage or loss to the unmanned aerial vehicle systems (aircraft structure).
- Material damage or loss to spare parts of the unmanned aerial vehicle systems.
- Legal liability to third parties.

: figure]

[FIGURE: logo: MEDGULF
ميدغلف MEDGULF

• **Engineering Insurance:**
The Engineering Insurance policy provides coverage for various risks linked to engineering projects, covering damages to properties, equipment, and machinery during construction, installation, maintenance, and more. Engineering insurance is essential for companies involved in engineering projects to protect themselves from unexpected expenses and legal claims. It offers a range of insurance coverages, including:

[FIGURE: Visual content: diagram]

[FIGURE: Central icon: Two hands holding a gear, with a stylized figure eight shape.]

[FIGURE: logo: MEDGULF
ميدغلف

- Group Life and Personal Accident Insurance:
The Group Life and Personal Accident Insurance policy ensures comprehensive insurance coverage against risks for employees in the event of death. The insurance coverage includes:

1Death Coverage (Illness or Accident):
The Death Coverage (Illness or Accident) policy ensures insured money is paid in case of death due to an accident or illness.

2Accident Death Coverage:
The Accident Death Coverage policy provides coverage to the insured in the event of death resulting from an accident, in addition to the coverage amount provided under the death insurance.

3Total Permanent Disability Resulting from Accident:
The Permanent Total Disability Resulting from Accident policy provides full compensation to the employee in the event of total disability due to an injury that prevents them from performing their job or performing any similar activities.

4Permanent Partial Disability Resulting from Accident:
The Partial Permanent Disability Resulting from Accident policy includes paying a percentage of the insurance amount to the insured based on a standard disability ratio schedule.

5Temporary Total Disability Resulting from Accident:
The Temporary Total Disability Resulting from Accident policy covers payment of a weekly salary to the insured in case of temporary total disability resulting from an accident.

6Medical Expenses due to Accident:
The Medical Expenses due to Accident policy covers actual medical expenses resulting from accidents up to a maximum of SAR 20,000.

7Chronic and Critical Illnesses:
The Chronic and Critical Illnesses policy covers payment of the insurance amount to the insured in case of suffering from chronic illnesses after the effective date of the insurance, up to 50% of the insurance amount.

8Permanent Total Disability due to Illness:
The Permanent Total Disability due to Illness policy covers payment of the full insurance amount in case of total disability of the employee resulting from an illness that prevents them from performing their job or performing any similar activities.

: figure]

<!-- PAGE BREAK -->

[FIGURE: logo: MEDGULF

# MEDGULF

The logo features the company name in English and Arabic, with a stylized book icon on the left and a thin line underneath the text.]

9Permanent Partial Disability due to Illness:
The Permanent Partial Disability due to Illness policy covers payment of a percentage of the insurance amount to the insured based on a standard disability ratio schedule.

10 - Embalming and Repatriation to the Home Country:
The Embalming and Repatriation to the Home Country policy covers the costs of embalming and transporting the insured's body to their home country.

11War Risks:
The War Risks policy covers the insured against damages and losses that may occur during times of war.

- Group Insurance Coverage for Borrowers from Banks and Financial Institutions:

The Group Insurance Coverage for Borrowers from Banks and Financial Institutions policy covers repayment of the loan
balance to the bank as of the date of death if the borrower's death is caused by an accident, illness, or total permanent
disability resulting from the accident or illness.

It covers:
1Death Coverage (Illness or Accident):
The Death Coverage (Illness or Accident) policy covers the loan balance for the insured in case of death, due to illness or accident.

## 2Permanent Total Disability Resulting from Accident:

The Permanent Total Disability Resulting from Accident policy covers the repayment of the loan balance in case of total disability resulting from an injury that prevents the insured from performing their profession.

## 3Permanent Total Disability Resulting from Illness:

The Total Permanent Disability Resulting from Illness policy covers the repayment of the loan balance in case of total disability resulting from an illness that prevents the insured from engaging in any occupation or profession.

## 4War Risks:

The War Risks policy covers the insured against war risks unless they are actively engaged in the war.

The reason of the increase (decrease) in revenues during the current year compared to the last year is | Insurance revenues increased during this year by SAR 689 million compared to last year, an increase of 26.07%. This is mainly due to the growth in Gross Written Premiums (GWP) of SAR 280.9 million, a growth of 9.84% which is driven by the strong performance of the health business line as it grew by 32.09% while a significant portion of the 2022 Motor Business was earned in 2023.
  3. The reason of the increase (decrease) in the net profit during the current year compared to the last year is | The company achieved net income before appropriation and zakat of SAR 206.255 million during the current year compared to a loss of SAR 405.856 million for the last year. The net income after Zakat amounted to SAR 201.472 million during the current year compared to loss of SAR 396.870 million for the last year, which was due to the following main reasons: -Improvement in insurance service result of SR 672.2 million compared with the previous year. This was driven by an increase in insurance revenue of SR 689.03 million, an increase of 26.07%, accompanied by a lower increase in the insurance service expense of 3.99% or SR 115.8 million, compared to the previous year, a direct result of the improved underwriting policy and cost containment. - Increase in net investment income in the profit and loss account of SAR 89.7 million compared to the previous year.
  4. Statement of the type of auditor&#x27;s report | Unmodified opinion
  5. Comment mentioned in the auditor&#x27;s report, mentioned in any of the following paragraphs (other matter, conservation, notice, disclaimer of opinion, or adverse opinion) | Attention is drawn to note 2 to the accompanying financial statements, which states that the Company did not meet the solvency margin requirements as at 31 December 2023. The deficiency in solvency margin indicates that a material uncertainty exists that may cast significant doubt on the Company&#x27;s ability to continue as a going concern. However, the accompanying financial statements are prepared using the going-concern assumption based on management&#x27;s assessment on the company&#x27;s abilities to continue as a going concern. The auditors&#x27; opinion is not modified with respect to this matter.
  6. Reclassification of Comparison Items | The Company has reclassified and restated comparative information to meet the requirements of the newly implemented standards IFRS 17 and IFRS 9.
  7. Additional Information | The company has adopted IFRS 17 (Insurance Contracts) and IFRS 9 (Financial Instruments), as endorsed in Saudi Arabia, starting 1 January 2023, with retrospective application which has materially changed the presentation of the financial results for periods starting Q1 2023 onwards with the comparative periods restated under the new standards. The earnings per share (EPS) for the current year are SR 1.92 against a SR 3.78 loss per share for the previous year which is calculated by dividing the net income amount of SR 201.5 million over the weighted average number of ordinary outstanding shares of 105 million for the current period and SR 396.8 million (loss) over 105 million shares for the previous year. The Company&#x27;s accumulated losses as of 31 December 2023 are 24.5%, an improvement of over 19pp over what it was at 31 December 2022 recording 43.7% of its subscribed capital and as of the same date, the Company&#x27;s solvency coverage is below the prudential solvency requirements. The solvency coverage now is exceeding 77% mark which is improved by more than 64pp compared to 31 December 2022.

Description of the Company's Profit Distribution Policy
Profit distribution policy identifies the Company's policy on distributing profits generated by business processes, in accordance with the company's by-laws, and by implementing applicable laws and regulations in the KSA:

Set aside the Zakat and income tax.

Set aside (20%) of the net profits to form a statutory reserve, Ordinary General Assembly may cease such deduction when the said reserve reaches the total paid-up capital.

Shareholders are entitled to receive their share of profits in accordance with the General Assembly resolution on this regard. General Assembly's decision identifies the due date and date of distribution. Only the shareholder listed in the shareholders record can receive profits on the due date.

Details of Shares and Debt Instruments Issued for Each Subsidiary
There are no shares or debt instruments issued to the subsidiaries.

## Details of Treasury Shares Held by the Company

There are no treasury shares owned by the Company.

Information relating to any competing business with the company or any of its activities that any member of the Board is engaging in or was engaging in such competing businesses.

As of the date of this filing, the company informs that there are no competing businesses for the company or any of the branches of the activity in which it is involved, and that none of the members of the Board of Directors are or were engaged in competing businesses.

- Conflict of interest cases and how they are handled: The company has established an executive approach to address potential conflicts of interest between its Board of Directors and executive management on one hand, and the company on the other hand, in order to ensure the best governance practices that protect shareholders' rights and interests. This is done in compliance with the applicable regulations and guidelines issued by the Capital Market Authority and the Insurance Authority. The company has developed several internal regulatory policies such as the disclosure policy, conflicts of interest policy, and governance regulations.

## Board of Directors:

*
The Board of Directors has the following duties and powers:

1.
To adopt and oversee the implementation of the company's trends, strategic plans, and main objectives, including the development of the company's overall strategy and main business plans, identification of the optimal capital structure and financial objectives of the company, supervision of the company's main capital expenditures, and the periodic review and approval of the company's organizational and functional structures.
2.
To develop policies and procedures to ensure the company's compliance with laws and regulations, as well as its obligation to disclose material information to shareholders, creditors and other stakeholders.
3.
To develop a company governance law that does not conflict with the regulations of the Capital Market Authority and the Saudi Central Bank, as well as supervise it, observe its effectiveness and amend it as necessary.
4.
To follow an obvious and transparent policy regarding share dividend distribution in a manner that achieves stakeholders and the company interests meanwhile.
5.
To develop a written policy that regulates the relationship with stakeholders to protect them and reserve their rights.
6.
To develop and oversee laws and controls for internal control, as well as supervise them.
7.
To supervise, approve, review and update all written policies and main procedures at the company on a regular basis.
8.
To adopt the committee's recommendation regarding the appointment of CEOs at the main centers and to

[FIGURE: logo: MEDGULF
ميدغلف
Blue and white text with a stylized arch symbol]

ensure that the company has a policy to replace a suitable alternative person with appropriate qualifications
and skills.
9To supervise the senior management and monitor company performance against the performance goals
set by the Board.

Listed below are the means by which the company evaluates the performance of its Board of Directors, its committees and members, as well as any external entity that is responsible for this evaluation and its relationship with the company, if applicable:

- Evaluation of the Performance of the Board of Directors and the Emanating Committees::
Each member of the Board of Directors or Committee shall be evaluated periodically to ensure that he/she complies with the standards and requirements defined in the specified procedures for Board membership. He/she must also comply with all laws, regulations, and instructions issued by the Saudi Central Bank (SAMA) and the Capital Market Authority (CMA).

The Nomination and Remuneration Committee shall evaluate the Board of Directors members as well as the entire Board of Directors, periodically (minimum once a year) in accordance with the confidentiality requirements of the evaluation.

The evaluation process shall be through a periodic evaluation for each Board of Directors member and the emanating committees, whereas the Nomination and Remuneration Committee members evaluate the Board of Directors members and its committees. While the chairman and other Board of Directors members evaluate the Nomination and Remuneration Committee members who are part of the Board of Directors.

In accordance with the evaluation policy, the Nomination and Remuneration Committee has applied the highest standards when evaluating each member separately, and has adopted updated forms for evaluating the Board of Directors' members, the emanating committees, and the Board in general.

Remuneration Paid to BOD Members and the Senior Executives of the Company (Including the CEO and CFO)
1Remuneration policy and method adopted to determine the remuneration of Board Members and Executive Management
- The company's Ordinary General Assembly, held on 25/03/2019G, approved the remuneration and compensation policy for BOD members, emanating committees and executive management, which is consistent with Article 19 of the company's Articles of Association:

A: Board of Directors: As part of the company's remuneration policy, the maximum total remuneration for the chairman and Board of Directors members shall not exceed SAR 500K for their membership on the Board and participation in its duties, including remuneration in the event the member participates in emanating committees, as follows:
*
BOD Chairman, SAR 260K annually.
*
BOD Vice-Chairman, SAR 230K annually.
*
BOD members, SAR 200K annually.
*
BOD Meetings attendance allowance, SAR 3K per meeting, provided that the number of meetings shall not exceed 10 meetings a year and shall not include accommodation and travel costs.

As part of the additional benefits, the BOD member and his family are provided with health insurance for the occupational risks they may face.

<!-- PAGE BREAK -->

[FIGURE: logo: MEDGULF
ميدغلف MEDGULF
Blue and gray text with a blue square and curved lines forming an abstract symbol]

Travel and Accommodation Costs: Remuneration in accordance with the company's travel rules policy.
The company's remuneration policy stipulates that if the company's dividends are used, it shall not exceed
10% of the company's net profits after deducting reserves and distribution of dividends to shareholders by at
least five percent (5%) of the company's paid-in capital, provided that this compensation is consistent with the
number of meetings attended by the member of the Board of Directors concerned.

B: Board of Directors Committee: Based on the Company's remuneration policy, the maximum total remuneration for the chairman and the Board members for their Board of Directors membership and their participation in its duties shall not exceed SAR 500K annually, including remuneration in cases where the member participates in the emanating committees as follows:

*
Committee chairman, SAR 100K annually.
*
Committee members, SAR 90K annually.
*
Committee Meetings attendance allowance, SAR 2K, provided that the number of meetings shall not exceed 10 meetings a year and shall not include accommodation and travel costs.

Board members and their families are provided with health insurance covering occupational risks as part of their additional benefits.

Travel and Accommodation Costs: Remuneration in accordance with the company's travel rules policy.

The annual remuneration value is divided into four (4) quarters.

## Your Responsibility

Blue and white logo with Arabic and English text, featuring a stylized 'M' symbol.]

List of Board Committees and duties:
The Board of Directors has established five committees to help it carry out its duties effectively. These are: the Audit Committee, the Nomination and Remuneration Committee, the Executive Committee, the Investment Committee, and the Risk Committee.

The Board of Directors reviews the committees' work periodically to ensure they are carrying out their assigned tasks. The committees also inform the Board of Directors periodically and in a transparent manner of what they do or reach from the results or what decisions they make. However, despite the formation of these committees, the final responsibility for the company rests with the Board of Directors.

Below is a brief explanation of the competencies of the aforementioned board committees, including their names, chairmen, members and the number of meetings they hold:

1Audit Committee:

The objectives of the audit committee are as follows:

*
Assisting the Board of Directors by monitoring the company's affairs and oversighting the adequacy of the internal control system and its effective implementation.
*
Reviewing the effectiveness of Internal Control System with Internal and External Auditors.
*
Reviewing the effectiveness of the company's automated system including IT security and controls.
*
Reviewing the effectiveness of the process for monitoring compliance with laws and regulations including company's policies and procedures.
*
Discussing the annual and interim Financial Statements with the External Auditors and the company's Senior Management and making the recommendations thereon to the Board of Directors.
*
Reviewing critical accounting policies and procedures as well as the modification that might be introduced thereto.
*
Instituting and overseeing special investigation in relation to fraud or any related matters that deems necessary to investigate.
*
Following-up the reports issued by Insurance Authority and other relevant supervisory and control entities.
*
Following-up on the lawsuits filed by or against the company.
*
Nominating the company's External Auditors that have the necessary experience in auditing Insurance and/ or Reinsurance Companies.
*
Reviewing the performance of Compliance and Internal & External Auditors and assess their independence and objectivity.
*
Monitoring the implementation of the Compliance and Internal Audit Plan and ensure no restrictions on their scope of work.

### Objectives and Functions:

*
To ensure the Board of Directors forms the 'Nominations and Remuneration Committee' and based on the Board's recommendations, the General Assembly issues the committee's work regulations, including the procedures, tasks, and regulations that govern the process of selecting committee members, their term of office, and determining their remuneration.
*
To ensure the Board of Directors and the Committee select and nominate members, ensuring the competency and suitability of candidates for board membership and senior management positions. Additionally, ensure they implement and oversee the compensation awarded to senior executives such as company directors and senior management members to motivate and keep them within the company.
*
Ensure that the Board of Directors maintains an appropriate structure, size and skills to support the strategic goals and values of the company.
*
Draw up the remuneration policy and supervising it for the members of the Board of Directors and the executive management to motivate and keep them within the company.
*
Supervise appointment procedures for leadership positions (including electoral processes) and succession plans.
*
Periodically review the remuneration policy and evaluating its effectiveness in achieving the desired goals, well as providing the necessary recommendations regarding remuneration policies and the framework for all company employees.
*
Provide the necessary recommendations to the Board of Directors regarding the appointment of members of the Board and its committees in accordance with the regulatory requirements, policies and approved standards.
*
Review the appropriate skills requirements for membership of the Board of Directors and its committees and preparing a comprehensive description of all capabilities and qualifications required for that membership, as well as determining the time that the member should allocate to the work of the Board of Directors and / or the committee, and this is done on an annual basis.
*
Periodically assess the structure and composition of the Board and its committees, identify weaknesses, and recommend corrective measures to be taken to address them, as necessary.
*
Evaluate the independence of board and committee members and ensure that there is no conflict of interest, including ensuring on an annual basis the independence of independent board and committee members.
*
Establish clear compensation and remuneration policies for board members, committees, and senior management members and presenting those policies to the board (the committee must make sure that these compensations are related to performance and ensure their application within the company).
*
Evaluate the performance of board members and committees on a regular basis.
*
Submit the necessary recommendations to the Board regarding the appointment and dismissal of members of higher management.
*
Establish succession policies and procedures for the CEO and senior members of senior management and monitor the implementation of succession plans and processes for them.
*
Periodically review compensation plans for members of senior management.
*
Provide the necessary recommendations to the Board of Directors on matters related to the nominations and remuneration of board members, committees and senior executives, in accordance with the approved policies.

: figure]

[FIGURE: logo: MEDGULF
ميدغلف
Blue and white text with a stylized arch symbol]

- Leadership Position Appointments:

- The company ensures that all appointments to leadership positions within its organisation are made only after assessing the suitability of the candidate in accordance with applicable requirements and obtaining a written non-objection from SAMA.

- The organization gives priority to the appointment of Saudi nationals to leadership positions within the company. In cases where there is a need to appoint a non-Saudi to a leadership position, the company must demonstrate the unavailability of a qualified Saudi candidate for the role. Nonetheless, the company establishes a timeframe for appointing qualified Saudi citizens to such positions in its request for a written non-objection from SAMA.

- The company establishes strict official policies and procedures to monitor and evaluate the suitability of board members, committees, and senior management for these positions, in accordance with SAMA's guidelines.

- The company must notify SAMA of any relevant information or circumstances related to reassessing the suitability of these individuals within a maximum period of three business days from the date of receiving the information or the date of the change.

- The company must obtain a written non-objection from SAMA before reassigning responsibility to any individual holding senior positions. The period for reassignment of responsibilities should not exceed six months and it can be renewed with the approval of SAMA.

- Candidates for senior positions assume their roles upon receiving a written non-objection from SAMA within five business days of contract termination, resignation, or appointment.

- Termination of the contractual relationship for individuals in senior positions is subject to the following conditions:
* Position holder resignation.
* Position holder death.
* Breach of obligations by the individual that results in harm to the interests of the company.
* Termination of the contract according to any applicable regulations or instructions in Saudi Arabia.
* If the individual is declared bankrupt or financially insolvent, files for settlement with creditors, or defaults on payment of their debts.
* In case the individual loses interest in the company's affairs.
* In case the individual is no longer mentally stable or fit to perform their duties.
* In case the individual is found guilty of committing an act of breach of trust and/or forgery.

3Investment Committee:
Objectives and Functions:

* Develop strategic plans for the company's investments and ensure their compliance with the provisions and conditions of the regulations and systems in force as well as conformity with the written policy that has been developed and duly approved by the Board of Directors.
* Supervise the implementation of the investment policy.
* Periodically review the investment policy and guidelines and issue new recommendations in line with market conditions.
* Provide written approval in cases that necessitate non-compliance with some conditions of the investment policy, and raise the issue, if necessary, to the Board of Directors.
* Approve of attractive investments and/or disposing of them.
* Approve the appointment of all asset managers to manage or advise on the company's assets.
* Review the report issued by the risk management department regarding the investment portfolio in order to ensure compliance with the approved policies and guidelines.
* Make final decisions regarding investments based on the recommendations of the Ministry of Finances.
* Monitor the performance of the company's investments, define the objectives and strategy of the investment, and set the necessary plans for its implementation.

5Risk Committee (BRC)
Key roles and responsibilities:

* Reviewing and endorsing risk appetite and setting the risk culture of MEDGULF.
* Reviewing MEDGULF Risk management frameworks and its infrastructure.
* Oversight over the Policy and SOP management framework including reviewing regular reports from Risk Management on the review cycles.
* Oversight investment risk management including capital adequacy and liquidity management.
* Review the proposed Risk Division strategy and plan for the coming year and ensure that it addresses key areas of risk. Assessment and monitoring, through periodic reports, the implementation of defined risk management strategies and policies and reviewing and updating them based on relevant internal and external changing factors.
* Ensure that risks beyond MEDGULF approved risk appetite reported by the Risk Division and management's proposed response/mitigation strategies are received, discussed and appropriately acted on.
* Reviewing the effectiveness of Company's business continuity including incident management.
* Reviewing that the Company's senior management continuously identify the risks that threaten the Company's existence and effectively identifies the risk exposures of the Company on regular basis.
* Overseeing the Company's risk management system and evaluating the effectiveness of the Company's systems and mechanisms for identifying and monitoring threats to the Company. Ensure that a formal communication process exists through which the Board and Senior Management are provided with sufficient information to assess the nature and level of, the Company's operational risk, through the sharing of operational risk reports to the Committee, and thereafter the Board or a regular basis.
* Advising the Board on issues related to risk management. BRC's minutes of the meeting should be presented to Board for their review. The next minutes of BRC meeting should contain reference to discussion with Board, if any, relating to issues of risk management.
* Examining any concerns raised by the Audit Committee, other Board Committees, or the Board itself that may have an impact on the Company's risk management activities.
* Reviewing that the Company's senior management is responsible for the Company's risk management processes and their effectiveness and give priority to discussions and actions dealing with risk management issues.
* Assessing the performance of Risk department periodically against the performance targets set at the beginning of the year.
* Reviewing the extent of compliance with regulations to determine what is the regulatory exposure and how it's being managed. Regulation includes all regulation, circulars, and frameworks.
* Oversight the cybersecurity function for the protection of information and information assets.
* Reviewing the actuarial function report at least annually.
* Review and approval of any decision specifically assigned to the Committee by the Board.
* Reviewing the recommendation or comments of risk management department over key transactions along with management action plan or comments, if any.
* Looking over reports on stress testing, such as the Capital & Adequacy report. This review would also look at any plans to improve the solvency, if there are any.

option (x): [ ] No Attendance;
option (-): [ ] Not Applicable due to membership expiry or non-commencement yet. | Name of Committee Member | 1st Meeting | 2nd Meeting | 3rd Meeting | 4th Meeting | |---|---|---|---|---| | Ms. Monirah Al-Suwidani | option 1st Meeting: [x] | option 2nd Meeting: [x] | option 3rd Meeting: [x] | option 4th Meeting: [x] | | Mr. Abdulaziz Al Zammam | option 1st Meeting: [x] | option 2nd Meeting: [x] | option 3rd Meeting: [x] | option 4th Meeting: [x] | | Mr. Faisal Al Jasser | option 1st Meeting: [x] | option 2nd Meeting: [x] | option 3rd Meeting: [x] | option 4th Meeting: [x] | ## Risk Management Initiatives

MEDGULF proactively implemented risk management practices in accordance with ISO 31000: Risk Management Guidelines and COSO ERM Framework. Implementing these frameworks can greatly enhance an organization's capacity to recognize, evaluate, handle, and oversee risks, ultimately facilitating better decision-making and strategic planning. In addition, this initiative enables MEDGULF to be fully compliant with Risk Management Regulation promulgated by regulatory authority, previously SAMA and current Insurance Authority (IA).

The key benefit which MEDGULF will reap from the initiative are given below:

## Strategic alignment

MEDGULF's risk management processes are fully aligned with its strategic goals, enabling effective strategic planning and objective setting that requires into account all potential risks. We have completed a thorough version of the Risk Strategy. Understanding the SWOT (Strengths, Weaknesses, Opportunities, and Threats) matrix is crucial for developing a solid risk strategy. This strategic planning tool helps organizations identify and analyze both internal and external factors that may affect their ability to achieve their objectives. When it comes to risk management, a SWOT analysis is essential for developing a strong risk strategy. It offers a structured approach to identify and evaluate both risks and opportunities.

[FIGURE: logo: MEDGULF
ميدغلف
Blue and white text with a stylized square and arched lines on the left]

## Risk assessment and risk response

An extensive exercise was conducted for every department within the Sector or Division to identify all the risks associated with each business process. Risks were identified based on the unique nature of the business processes, industry practices, and regulatory requirements. Every risk was evaluated based on risk assessment criteria, which considers the potential impact in terms of financial, legal and compliance, operational, reputation, and governance factors.

Preparing a risk response and risk treatment strategy involves a disciplined approach. This includes identifying all stakeholders and determining their responsibilities in responding to risk. It also involves having thorough discussions with business owners and the risk team. Additionally, regular monitoring of internal and external factors that could impact the risk profile is necessary, along with the need to revise risk ranking or response as needed.

Performance improvement
Through the integration of risk management into business processes at all levels, these frameworks have the potential to improve performance and efficiency, minimizing unexpected setbacks and losses. An incident management framework was operationalized and enhanced during the year. Business owners aligned with risk management to identify operational or financial incidents and reported them to the risk team using a standardized template. This ensured that all aspects of the incidents were covered and focused on, with the goal of avoiding or minimizing their occurrence in the future.

## Enhanced governance

It encourages stronger governance structures by clearly defining roles and responsibilities related to risk management, thus encouraging accountability and transparency. The following measures have either been implemented or are currently being worked on:

* The risk operating model has been finalized. This includes the three lines of defense model, risk management lifecycle, and regulatory requirements. By reflecting all these elements, it becomes possible to clearly identify and differentiate the roles and responsibilities of each stakeholder.
* Articulated to roles and responsibilities of stakeholders (Board of Directors, Executive Management, Board Risk Committee and Risk Management Division) up to the level of each risk management component such as risk strategy, risk policies, risk SOPs, and operating model.
* Identification of risk champion across all sectors / divisions of MedGulf.

# Compliance

The frameworks help organizations to comply with applicable laws, regulations, and standards, thereby avoiding fines and penalties and enhancing the organization's reputation.

<!-- PAGE BREAK -->

[FIGURE: logo: MEDGULF

# MEDGULF

The logo features the company name in English and Arabic, with a stylized book icon on the left and a thin line underneath the text.]

I. Human Resources Risks

The insurance market needs qualified personnel familiar with insurance activity, which increases demand and exposes the company to risk of moving its qualified personnel, especially in light of resettlement requirements. However, the company continues to train and qualify current and future employees in a variety of ways to suit various management levels. Despite losing some human resources to competing parties, this decision is in the country's best interest. All company divisions and administrative levels will continue to build Saudi national competencies.

## II. Market and Competition risks

The insurance business is highly competitive, which may affect the company's activity and future opportunities and lead to price competition. With intense competition from other insurance companies, the company has taken a series of proactive actions based on offering competitive prices, based on statistical and actuary basis, ensuring the safety and success of technical capabilities for underwriting insurance policies, and effective preventive programs to grow and achieve its objectives.

### III. Information Technology Risks

IT risk refers to the potential for loss, damage, or destruction of assets as a result of a threat exploiting a vulnerability within the information technology environment of an organization. It encompasses a wide range of issues related to information security, data integrity, operational continuity, and compliance. These risks can manifest from various sources, including cyber-attacks, data breaches, system failures, human error, and natural disasters.

There are range of mitigation measures to mitigate these risks, key measures are given below:

* All the changes in the existing systems are undertaken through following a change management process, which ensures that all the changes are properly logged, implemented timely and tested before going live.
* MedGulf maintains proper disaster recovery sites which maintain the replica of all critical business applications. The functionality of this site has is tested within IT department.
* Data backup is maintained regularly on daily, weekly and monthly basis. In the case of any unforeseen event, data can be recovered from the backups.
* To safeguard network, prioritize strong password policies and multi-factor authentication. Implement firewalls and anti-malware software, keeping them updated. Regularly patch systems and monitor network activity for suspicious behavior.

IV. Insurance Risks

Insurance risks involve contracting parties' claims for insured events exceeding the book value of insurance obligations. The Company's main goals are to ensure adequate resources to meet these obligations:

: figure]

[FIGURE: logo: MEDGULF
ميدغلف MEDGULF
Blue and white logo with Arabic and English text, featuring a stylized 'M' or arch-like symbol to the left of the text.]

*

## Health Insurance

The Company's health insurance plan diversifies risk type and insured benefits. The diversity of sectors and geographical areas ensures that prices consider current health conditions, the usual review of actual claims and the product's price, according to the actuary's pricing schedules, as well as detailed claim follow-up procedures. The firm also takes claims seriously and actively to cover unforeseen future risks.

*

## Motor Insurance

Motor insurance risks include loss, injury, and vehicle replacement or repair. The company only issued comprehensive insurance policies to owners or drivers over 18 years old and adhered to the actuary's pricing schedule to reduce such risks. Most vehicle insurance contracts are with people.

*
Duplication and Amounts of Claims

Numerous variables can affect claim duplication and quantities, and these operations are considered short-term insurance contracts. Typically, claims payments are reported within a year of an insured incident, which reduces insurance risk.

• Sensitivity analysis
The company considers that the amounts of outstanding claims according to the insurance contracts at the end of the year are adequate; however, these amounts are uncertain and may differ from the amounts reported in the financial statements. The insurance claim quantities are subject to multiple assumptions. As the insurance claims provision is influenced by the aforementioned fundamental assumptions, it is impossible to determine the sensitivity of certain variables, such as legislative changes or evaluation process uncertainty.

V. Reinsurance Risks

Like other insurance firms, the company reinsures with third parties during its normal business cycle to reduce financial losses from large insurance claims. These arrangements ensure company variety, allow management to control potential losses from huge risks, and provide additional growth capabilities to reduce its exposure to huge losses from reinsurer bankruptcy. Reinsurance firms' financial health and international rankings are important to the company. The company is obligated to policyholders with its share of outstanding reinsured claims to the extent that the reinsurance company did not fulfill its obligations under the assigned reinsurance agreements.

VI. Risks of investment Returns

The company's financial results depend in part on how well its investments perform. The company's returns on investments and, by extension, its profitability may be adversely affected from time to time by things that affect specific investments and, more generally, by changes in the market and the economy that are out of the company's control. A lot of what the company does also rests on how the economy is doing in Saudi Arabia and around the world.

<!-- PAGE BREAK -->

[FIGURE: logo: MEDGULF

# MEDGULF

Logo features the company name in English and Arabic, with a stylized 'M' or book icon on the left, all in dark blue.]

## VII. Credit Risks

Credit risk is the inability of one party to meet its obligations, resulting in a financial loss to the other party, for all categories of financial assets acquired by the Company, with the company's maximum credit risk corresponding to the book value disclosed in the financial position list. The company implements a number of policies and procedures to mitigate the credit risk to which it is exposed, such as the following:

- All customers with whom the business intends to conduct business are subject to credit checks and analysis. In addition, the company monitors the balance due under insurance and reinsurance contracts on an ongoing basis to reduce its exposure to bad debt risks.
- The Company will reduce the risks associated with agents and brokers by establishing credit limits for each agent and broker and closely monitoring overdue receivables.
- The company attaches great importance to the adherence to the credit policy and the collection of these amounts due to the company.
- The company's investment portfolio is managed by the investment officer in accordance with the investment policy adopted by the Investment Committee.
- The company enters into reinsurance contracts only with internationally recognized and ranked entities.
- With regard to credit risk arising from other financial assets, the company deals only with commercial banks with a strong financial position and good credit reputation.
- The company ensures that there are no concentrations of credit risk with any party

VII. Regulatory and Legal Risks

The Insurance Authority (IA) oversees the company's insurance products and operations through the cooperative insurance control law and regulation and the Council of Health Insurance (CHI) executive regulation for health insurance products. Insurance sector structure and supervision generally favor insured and investors. The non-compliance with these laws and regulation may harm the company's business, finances, and operations. Thus, these risks relate to the company's commitment to all legislation, regulations, and laws issued by regulatory and official authorities, considering the multiplicity of relevant regulatory and supervisory bodies, the speed of regulation and legislation development, and the extent of their applicability in the insurance market that may affect insurance companies in the event of non-compliance with changes in regulations and laws. These regulations require approvals, control, and capital adequacy requirements to lower insurers> risk of deficit and bankruptcy and allow them to meet their obligations. A specialized department monitors the company's compliance with laws and regulations and implements processes to comply with all present and future laws and regulations.

VIII. Liquidity Risks

Liquidity risks are financial obligations that a company cannot fulfill in a timely manner without incurring negative consequences. Periodically, the company monitors its liquidity requirements. In addition, it assures sufficient liquidity to meet obligations as they arise. In addition, the company evaluates its capital requirements to maintain the financial solvency rate mandated by regulatory authorities.

[FIGURE: logo: MEDGULF
ميدغلف
The logo features the company name in English and Arabic, with a blue rectangular graphic containing a wave-like pattern to the left of the English text.]

IX. Foreign Currency Risks
Risks associated with the fluctuating value of a financial instrument due to variations in the foreign exchange rate constitute currency risks. Due to the fact that the majority of the company's transactions are conducted in Saudi Riyals (SAR), the management believes there is a low risk of significant loss due to changes in the foreign exchange rate. Therefore, the corporation does not provide coverage for foreign currency risks.

X. **Risks of Private Commission Rates**

Private commission rate risks result from discrepancies in the value or future cash flows of a financial instrument as a consequence of market-wide changes in private commission rates. Private commission rates pose a threat to the company's investments in cash, quasi-cash, and term deposits. Monitoring changes in private commission rates for currencies in which the company's investments are registered reduces such risks.

XI. Capital Management Risks

Insurance Authority defines and regulates capital requirements. In order to maintain balanced capital ratios and increase shareholder interest, the company establishes additional objectives. The company manages its capital requirements by evaluating the difference between the announced and required levels of capital. All settlements shall be based on the current capital levels, in accordance with changes in market conditions and risk characteristics of the company's activities, as well as the maintenance or modification of capital structure.

XII. Operational Risks

Operational risks are loss risks caused by control or system failure, such as human error or theft. These hazards could result in financial losses, reputational damage, regulatory and legal consequences. The company manages operational risks through the implementation of appropriate controls, separation of duties, internal monitoring, and risk management. Given the expansion of the project, it is also intent on maintaining operational standards.

XIII. **Business Continuity Risks**
The company is committed to maintaining work continuity and preventing the risks most likely to disrupt it. In accordance with risk management regulation requirements issued by the Insurance Authority (IA)., the company began developing an emergency plan for all divisions, outlining the procedures and steps to be taken to ensure the correct progression of key activities.

XIV. Underwriting Risks

Such risks are reflected in the company's pricing risks and geographical and qualitative concentration of underwritten risks. Accordingly, it developed precautionary measures, including a pricing strategy informed by actuarial data. This strategy is periodically reviewed and revised in accordance with the evolution of company's business plan, market behavior, and applicable laws. The company also began establishing an underwriting strategy across its divisions, reflecting its underwriting policy and technical vision.

: figure]

<!-- PAGE BREAK -->

[FIGURE: logo: MEDGULF

# MEDGULF

Logo features the company name in English and Arabic, with a stylized 'M' or book icon on the left, all in dark blue.]

• Audit Committee Report:

The Audit Committee is dedicated to reviewing the Compliance, Internal and External Auditors assessment of internal control procedures, including the deficiencies in the general structure and performance of internal control systems, in order to ensure the effectiveness and efficiency of the system by verifying the implementation of regulated policies and procedures, as well as compliance with applicable laws and regulations in Saudi Arabia.

The Audit Committee has called to order 10 meetings in 2023 in order to fulill its role and duties, where key stakeholders and members of the company's management attended each meeting, along with the company's external auditors. As a result, various members of the management have provided input to the Committee regarding the integrity, effectiveness and accuracy of the company's financial statements, compliance with applicable laws and regulations, assessment of internal control, risk-based and regulatory-based internal audits, as well as management of operational and financial risks.

## Internal Control Procedures

Based on input and presentations from relevant key stakeholders, the Audit Committee has evaluated and received report on a number of key issues, including:

* Interim and annual financial statements.
* Establishment of effective internal controls and procedures to ensure compliance with accounting standards, financial reporting procedures and applicable laws and regulations.
* Compliance observations report including regulators' observation.
* Annual internal audit report activities.
* Company code of conduct.
